Then administer medicines that promote the growth of new flesh where it is healthy.
And Al-Bukasi says that the gist of what we have narrated is simply that some people have seen patients who have suffered from this type of abscess and the patient has died, and the flesh has become necrotic, and some try to insert a tube into the glottis so that the patient can breathe through the wound to save them from death.
And for this reason he commanded that the wound be left open until the evil of the illness is consumed, and its evil lasts three days; then afterwards, he commanded to sew up the wound, and heal it once it is healthy.
And what I have seen with my own eyes is that a servant held a hot cloth to his throat and inserted the end of a cane into his glottis, and I was called to treat him; then I discovered the abscess and found blood which had oozed from the abscess.
Then he confessed that he hadn't pierced any vein or artery; rather, the pus had come out of the abscess and I treated it until it was healed.
And the servant didn't feel any pain except when he spoke; then after a few days he returned to his usual state.
And now I say that in the section of the glottis there is no fear.
Chapter 44.
Of an incision on an abscess which occurs in the exterior glottis and is called a glottal hernia.
This hernia of the glottis is a large abscess according to the colour of the body and occurs in women.
And it occurs in two ways: either naturally or accidentally.
The natural type is incurable.
And the accidental type occurs in two ways: one is like fatty lumps and the other type is like an abscess caused by arterial congestion; there is danger in that. And do not use a needle on it unless it is small. And examine it and investigate it with your finger, and if you find it like a fatty lump and not suspended by any vein, then pierce it in the same way as nodules; extract its contents along with the skin and bursa; otherwise, probe throughout its entire extent, and treat the area with something that promotes healing until it is healthy.
Chapter 45.
Of incisions on nodules.
Nodules have different types and I have already discussed all of their types in Division.
And you should also know the difference between a nodule and an ulcer if you are in doubt.
Therefore I say that an ulcer is hot and painful with a violent fever until the ebullition of the superfluity ceases; then when the fever, pain, and heat cease, it is complete putrefaction.
But a nodule does not have heat or fever or pain, and it contains the lion's tooth which is a proper sac.
And it is according to the colour of the body; its beginning is with a boil and it is caused in the same way as a boil, whether major or minor; and there are two types, either fatty and containing humidity, and the colours of humidity vary, as I discussed in Division.
Therefore, when you come to treat a nodule, open it and probe its beginning with the instrument that is called an introducer, according to the form that will appear in the chapter that follows.
And this is the way to probe abscesses and all nodules: take this instrument and insert it into the moist part which you find in the abscess, and rotate your fingers with it little by little until you know that the instrument has penetrated the edge.
Then close your hand around it according to the size of the abscess; then extract the introducer and examine what has oozed from it.
And if the pus is flowing out, whatever its colour, then you shall pierce it superficially as I have said regarding other abscesses.
And if there is no pus flowing from the introducer, then you shall know that it is fatty.
And dry it by piercing in a cross shape according to this shape: And if it is fatty and dry, then you shall dry it by cutting the sac of the nodule.
But if it is ruptured in the operation, then it is not possible to extract that pus; rather, many times it goes back inside, and then you shall extract it in small amounts until it doesn't go back inside for any reason.
For if from it anything goes back inside, little or a lot, the nodule returns according to the cause.
And if you see that anything small goes back inside, then complete the wound with some sharp corrosive powders and strengthen the wound, and place your hand over it so that there is no abscess; then heal it by another treatment until it is healthy.
And if it is a large nodule, then cut its two lips and heal it with that which makes it grow inside.
But if there is a pulsating vein on it, or a non-pulsating one, then bind and fill the area with bloodletting that is mild and let it flow for two or three days until the wound stops ebullition and the blood; then return to piercing where it has ruptured.

Of section of apostemes that happen by artery or vein.

Chapter .22.
Of outstanding cure of the navel.
Eminence of the navel is made for several reasons; or through fissures of the abdomen which is over the belly, and there of it the tissue or intestine according to where it goes into other ruptures; or by blood which flows from artery or vein according to what is in front, or by constriction narrowed on it.
But if it is through fissure of the abdomen and by moisture of the tissue, then the color of the ulcer is similar to the color of the body; and there is little pain in it, and then appears from diverse locations. And if it is by passage of the intestine, then the location of that with respect to what we have told you is very violent, and when you press that with your fingers there is hiding, and then it returns; and it is very strong in it, and it is magnified much because of the intake of bath and violent work.
But if it is by moisture, then there is little pain and it is not hidden when you press with your hand, nor is constricted, nor is burned.
And if it is by blood, then with these signs appears the ulcer declining to blackness.
But if it is by flesh, then there is grave ulcer, large and hard, and it is made according to a quantity.
But if it is by constriction, then the touch of it is painful.
And the operation on it is that you consider if the eminence of the navel is by blood from artery or vein, or through constriction; then there is a prohibition against its cure, for in that one is fear and dread as we taught in the chapter in which we said about ulcers by artery and by vein.
Here is my translation: "And if the protrusion of the navel is by the intestine or by the hernia, then you should order the patient to hold his breath and be standing upright; and then sign with your finger around the entire navel, and order him to lean forward between your hands on his chest, and then surround with a wide sponge around the navel where you have signed with your finger; and then extend half of the abscess to the parts above with a large needle; and then bind around with strong thread or with linen in the decent manner of binding."
And then cut the membrane of the extended abscess over the ligament and insert your finger into that place and seek the intestine; and if you have caught it or held it by the ligament, then you extract it quickly and push the intestine back inside the abdominal cavity.
And if you have caught the hernia, then take hold of it with a needle; and pierce the superfluities of it.
But if it is contrary to your artery or vein, then surround that spot and then return to your operation; and take two needles and put on them two strong threads and insert the two needles around the circuit which you have made around the abscess in the manner of a cross, making the needles penetrate; and then tighten the abscess in four parts over the needles.
And if you wish, remove the needles and let the flesh extend and fall by itself; or pierce what is sottile and let it be healed with water that is warm enough to heal the wound.
And if the protrusion of the navel is from meat in him or from humidity, then you should reduce the abscess as we have said and draw out the blood or humidity which you find in it, and then heal that with water that covers and hardens the spot.
Chapter 53:
Of the cure for a hernia.
We have already said, in the division, about the kind of hernia and how it is healed by medicines, and that it is to be cured by iron if it is not ulcerated; we have also said where a hernia is generated and what are its precautions for curing it.
And the ancients said that sometimes a hernia can be in a place where its removal is possible, like one in the breasts or in the groin and similar places of the limbs, and they are inclined to extract all of it, especially when it begins small.
But when it is old and large, then one should not touch it, for I have not seen anyone healed of such nor have I heard of anyone being healed.
And the operation on it, when it is located as we have said, is that you precede and let the patient fast and purge black bile sometimes, and then bleed him if there is found a full pulse.
And then prepare the patient with a preparation in which he is located for operation, and then push in nails into the wound which cover that; and then hollow out every part with a good saw without piercing any root of it. And let the blood flow and do not cut it off quickly, and squeeze out the places and wipe away the clotted blood with your hand or with an instrument by which it is possible for you to do so.
But if it causes you distress of clotted blood from a vein or artery, then cauterize that until the flow of blood is stopped and then heal that with the other cure until it is healed.
Chapter 54:
Of the cure for dropsy.

But if you see the patient with abundant strength and there is no other illness in him but dropsy alone, and he is not an infant or old, then the manner of operating on him is that you elevate the patient between your hands and the minister then squeeze his abdomen with his hand, pushing out the water to the part below the navel, and then take a pointed sponge according to this form:

But evacuate from that according to the quantity of the strength of him and according to what signifies to you the dispositions of the strength of his pulse and of his goodness.
And then extract the instrument and remove the water which causes it for as soon as it is removed the membrane which holds it, you have recommended to pierce that according to that manner.
And then return the instrument on the other day if you see the patient tolerating that, and extract from the water a little quantity and do that for several days over fear, and beware of error so that it does not burst with too much water.

And beware in your operation of flowing blood, for sometimes this happens; and place on him that which stops the blood, and heal the wound until it is healed.
Chapter 56.
Of whitening which happens in the foreskin on the head of the penis, and of corruption and blackness, and adhesion of the foreskin to the head of the penis.

Chapter 57.
Of the purification of children and the cure of what happens to those who are circumcised.
Circumcision is not a cure of continence like the other wounds: but however it is from our operation and our will, and its use is more properly in children; therefore we should assign to it better operation and by a longer way lose less health.
Therefore we say that the ancients did not prescribe circumcision in any of their free ones, because they do not use it in their laws, and it is only because we have acquired through experience, which cause is that we have observed the greatest part of the artisans and barbers using circumcision and purification with a knife and with torches; and they use adhesive with pitch and incision with the nail.
And I have already proven all these manners and not found better purification with forceps, with adhesive with pitch that in purification with the nail, because sometimes the thread escapes above, because the thread of the foreskin is on two tunics, and the tunic pushes from below, and it is very likely to another incision and sure pain. And with purification which is made by aphexin, and it is digital, of which the sabatiers use, is not secure the incision of the extremity of the male member, because it often enters in its wound.
But in the operation with the nail, very often you will get iron and corrupt your operation. And the thread of the child is short by nature, and sometimes it happens in such a way that he has not needed purification, and I have seen this.
But of the purification which is made by forceps and adhesive with pitch, the goodness, I have discovered through experience that the forceps are equally proportional incision, therefore that the acuteness which is above is also with the acuteness which is below; and then when you measure your hand so proportionally two acuteness, and insert according to a comparison in one time; and it is made compression of the pitch which contains the figure containing the thread of the penis from all sides, with which there is no error at all.
And the manner of the first operation is that you make the child lie down mostly if he is one of those who understand a little, and do not but that you tie the pitch in his penis only, and then let him lie for another day.
And then make him cheer up in all that way which is possible for you by receiving his intelligence. Then have the patient lie between your knees, fully exposed and not covered; hide the forceps in your hand or under your foot so that the child does not see them or any of the other instruments.
Then insert your hand into the vagina and blow into the cervix, and draw out whatever is inside so that the head of the cervix comes out, and then clean it of any dirt that has accumulated there.
The shape of the forceps for cleaning, this is their shape:
Let one end of the forceps be blunt and the other pointed, so that the nerve in the claw is not cut; and let the length of both jaws be equal to the length of two fingers joined together.
The mistake in cleaning is that often the cervix itself escapes completely, or part of it escapes from the incision.
Therefore, you must carefully insert your finger into the aperture and push it forward until you feel resistance, then insert the forceps according to its equal length.
And if you cannot hold it with your finger, then grab it with a hook and insert it.
But if it has passed three days, and the swelling under the cervix remains, then you must insert it so that the apostome gives way, and cut it out easily, and insert it according to how it is prepared for you.
And beware of the head of the cervix, for it will not tolerate that.
And so treat that with the powders we have recounted in the treatise on powders, to promote healing.
And if it is cut beyond measure, and obeys the rules above, then it will be fine.
But treat that with what we have said earlier, so that it heals.
Chapter .LVIII.
Of the treatment of urine retained in the bladder.
Retention of urine in the bladder is caused by obstruction caused by a stone, or by congealed blood, or by swelling or by growths; and it is treated similarly to what we have said about treatments in the division above.
And if it is not dissolved by what we have said earlier and the cause of it is vehement upon the patient, then have extraction performed on him with an instrument called a syringe, of which this is the form: Let it be made of silver and let it be hollow like a reed made of aspen wood with a slender hole in its tip, about the thickness of a long finger, to which there is attached a slender cane about the length of a palm and a half, to whose end there is attached a hollow cane.
And the method of removing urine with it is to take the thread and soak it in the end of the syringe in wool or cloth with a good grip; and insert the ends of the thread into the opening at the tip of the syringe, and with the forceps, if there is any excess caused by the wool, but otherwise insert it into the cane with force. Then push the syringe in with force and with the white of an egg.
And have the patient lie down on his back, and open his bladder and cervix with oils, and olive oil and water.
Then insert the syringe with ease until it reaches the root of the cervix; then bend the cervix above at the point of the embelic; and squeeze the syringe within that; and squeeze it until it reaches the bladder, and let the patient be bent so that the cause is vacated, and not done according to this order, but the part in which there is tortuosity.
Then slowly pull out the thread with the wool, for the urine will suck up the wool.
Then pull it out and let the urine be passed through treatment; use the syringe, do not stop using it until the bladder is evacuated and the patient feels relief.
Chapter .LIX.
Of the quality of catheterization of the bladder with a syringe and similar instruments that are suited to it.

Therefore, when you want to inject fluid into the bladder, insert the tip of the syringe into the opening, and push with that which is pushed from above, for the fluid is drawn up into the hollow of the syringe.
Then insert the tip of the syringe into the cervix according to what we have said about the syringe; and squeeze the fluid with that which is squeezed, for that fluid will pass at once into the bladder, and the patient will feel it.
Form of the hollow needle with which the bladder is catheterized, and this is its form:
And let it be made of silver or brass, the tip of which is like a little feather, and below that there is a cane.

Chapter 60.
Of the Extraction of Stone.
We have already spoken in the division of the species of stone and its cure by medicine, and the difference between stone generated in the kidneys and stone generated in the bladder, and their signs.
And we have spoken of the stone for which cauterization is used, and incision.
And the stone generated in the bladder properly speaking is that which is lodged in the bladder.
And I have given an explicit account and summary of this.
Therefore I say that stone generated in the bladder mostly affects children; and of its signs are that the urine which is passed from the bladder is like water in its thinness, and appears to be sand; and the patient grinds his loins, and often passes water, and is frequently erect; and with this there are pains in many parts of the body.
And the cure is easier in children who have reached the age of 14; and it is difficult to cure the old. But in the young it may be cured by cauterization, which is suitable for them.
And if the stone is large and its cure more difficult, then it is otherwise.
Therefore when we come to the cure of this, it is advisable at the beginning that we cleanse the patient by cauterization in order to open up the passage which is in his intestines; for this passage sometimes blocks the expulsion of the stone as a result of the examination.
And then let him be placed on his feet and made to move about and jump up and down in order that the stone may descend into the bottom of the bladder, or that it may drop out by itself at some other place.
And then let the patient lie on his back with his thighs drawn up and his legs bent under him, in order that the whole bladder may be made to decline towards its lower parts.
And then let him void all of this.
Therefore if you feel the stone in the passage, then immediately cauterize it there.
And if it does not come out by itself, then let you smear your left forefinger with oil (if the patient is a child) or your middle finger (if he is grown up), and insert that into his anus. And push the stone out by means of your finger. And gradually draw it into the neck of the bladder.
And then press on that with your finger and expel it through the lower opening by means of the place where you cauterized.
And order the assistant to press on the bladder with his hand; and order another assistant that with his right hand to extend the scrotum upwards, and with his other hand to massage the cord which is below the scrotum in the place where you are cauterizing.
And then insert a piece of sponge in the passage, the shape of which is as follows: and cut through it where it is between the anus and scrotum, not in the middle part, but on the left side of the scrotum; and let the cauterization be over that stone, and let your finger be in the anus, and let the incision be transverse so that the opening outwards may be wide and the opening inwards narrow according to the amount of stone which can be expelled without difficulty, and not larger, for fear it should close up again.
And take note that some stone has corners and edges, in consequence of which the expulsion is made difficult thereby.
And some are like a onion, round and easy to expel.
Therefore if it is one of those which have corners and edges, adjust the cautery in the fissure.
And if it is not expelled, then let you press on that, or that you press upon it gently with a suitable instrument, the end of which is curved, and do not allow it to slip out; or insert below it a thin instrument with a curved end.
But if you cannot reach it, then let you enlarge the hole a little, and if you see any bleeding, bind up that tightly with powdered vitriol.
But if it is larger than one, then at the beginning push your finger towards the mouth of the bladder, and then insert a small instrument into it; and act in the same way if there are more than two.
And if the stone is very large, then it is foolishness to insert it with a wide incision, for two causes may occur: either it will stay there or it will cause continuous discharge of urine, because the passage has not healed completely.
But let the assistant expel it once it is pushed out, or force it in the fracture with pincers in order to extract that into pieces.
Therefore when you have finished your operation, then fill the wound with cotton wool soaked in aloe and dragon's blood, and bind it up tightly. And place over that a cloth which has been dipped in oil and wine, or in rose oil and water, in order that the wound may heal quickly.
And then bind up the patient over his navel, and do not loosen the bandage for three days.
And when you have loosened it, wash the wound with water and oil, and then cure that with ointment of diaphenicon and ointment of diabasilicon until it is healed.
But if in the wound there occurs an abscess, hard and ulcerous, and this is like a congelation of the blood in the bladder so that passage of urine is prevented  (and this is called by some the exit of blood through the urethra), then let you insert your finger into the wound and extract that blood, for if it becomes putrid and rotten it will provoke corruption of the bladder.
And then wash the wound with sweet wine, water and salt, and apply all remedies which seem suitable for its cure until it is healed.
And throughout the whole of the cure let you press both scrota and apply remedies which are laid on the wound.
And if the stone is small and lodged in the middle of the urethra so that passage of urine is prohibited, then cure it by cauterizing there, for troops have often been seen to be cured by this cure; and I have also tried it, and it has been found effective, and you should use a piercing instrument of iron, the shape of which is as follows:
triangular in cross-section, pointed, set in a handle.
And then take a hammer and hit the urethra below the stone so that it does not return to the bladder.
And then insert the iron into the urethra, piercing with ease so that the piercing instrument reaches that stone. And turn the piercing instrument with your hand on that small stone little by little, and pierce through it so that you make the passage on the other side as well, for urine is immediately expelled.
And then press your hand over that which is broken from the stone in the passage of the urethra, for it is clenched and the passage is closed by the urine, and the patient is cured.
But if this cure is not equipped for some cause which prevents it, then strike a hammer below the stone and another hammer above it. And then close upon that stone in the urethra between two ligatures. And then you extract it. Then cut the ligament and clean the clotted blood that has accumulated in the wound.
And it is not necessary to cut the ligament of the gallbladder below the stone, but so that it does not return to the bladder; and the other ligament above, for when the gallbladder is removed and the stone comes out, the bladder returns to its place and the wound heals.
And for this reason, when you tie the gallbladder above, you must lift the bladder up to the opening above, or it will return to its original position and the wound will not heal as we have said.
Chapter 61:
On the extraction of stones from women.
Stones are rarely formed in women.
However, if a stone is found in one of them, then its cure is difficult and prohibited by many methods.
One of these is that the woman is very young.
And the second is that you do not find a woman who is willing to reveal if she has had sexual intercourse or is married.
The third is that you cannot find a woman skilled in this art, especially one who performs the operation with her hands.
And the fourth is that the site of incision for removing a stone in women is distant from the location of the stone; therefore, it requires a long incision, and there is fear in that.
However, if necessity compels you to do this, then know that you must take a female doctor who is very skilled, and she is rarely found.
But if you lack such a woman, then seek a subtle and skilled male doctor, or present a female midwife who is experienced in the affairs of women, or a woman who has some knowledge of this art.
Then have her present and command him to do everything that you tell him, from the examination for the stone to the beginning; the purpose of this is to determine whether the woman is a virgin, then have her insert her finger into the anus and feel for the stone.
Then if she finds it, hold it back with her finger, and then command him to insert his hand into her.
But if she is not a virgin, then command the midwife to insert her finger into the vagina and feel for the stone; then have her pause her left hand over the bladder and press it firmly with good grip.
Then if she finds it, then have her gradually push the stone from the opening of the bladder to the parts below until it comes out at the root of the thigh.
Then insert your finger into the vagina above the root of the thigh from whichever side it is found, and center the stone in that part, and his finger should not be pushed back by the stone as he holds it.
And the incision should be small at first; then insert your finger into that incision and if he feels the stone, then widen the incision according to the size of the stone he knows will come out.
And know that there are many kinds of stones: some are small and large, smooth and rough, long and round, and they have projections.
Therefore you should know how many types there are so that you can indicate what you want.
And if you see bleeding, apply crushed vitriol to the wound and hold it there for an hour until the bleeding stops; then return to your operation and finish removing the stone.
And prepare the instruments which you use in extracting stones from men, so that you may be assisted by them in your operation.
And if you see bleeding and know that the flow of blood is from an artery that has been cut, then you must pause powder over the wound and bind it tightly with a bandage; do not repeat this; remove the stone and do not extract it, for the patient will surely die. Then heal the wound.
So when the sharpness of the bleeding has ceased and the wound is closed, then return to your operation and finish removing the stone.
Chapter 62:
On incision for hernia in women.
Hernia is nothing but an accumulation of moisture in the white membrane below the diaphragm that contains the bowels; it is named ciphax.
And in some cases it is in the lower part of the peritoneum that nature prepares it in the part of the bowels where there are other bowels; and it is the diaphragm below the white membrane that we have said earlier, and it is not anything else but hernia.
And the generation of this hernia is due to weakness that occurs in the bowels, because this matter flows into them; and sometimes it occurs due to a blow made on the bowels.
And this moisture has many colors; for the color of it is either inclining towards yellowish or blood-red, or red, or is dark and foul, or it is watery white, and that is what is most common.
And the signs by which one knows that this accumulation of moisture is in the white diaphragm that we have said earlier are: for if it is in the white diaphragm, then the hernia is round and declining a little towards length with the figure of the bowels, and covering the bowel; for the moisture contains all around.
And if the moisture is in the peritoneum itself, then the hernia is round with the part of the bowels and one estimates that it is another bowel.
And if the moisture is between the diaphragm of the bowels and the white diaphragm, then cut below the center.
And when you want to know the color of the moisture, then test the color of the moisture in the hernia with a needle from which the thread has been removed; and according to what is seen in the marks of the needle, judge what is inside it.
Therefore when we come to the treatment of it with iron, then have the patient lie on his back if that is possible for him, and see his chest.
Then let him be reclined on his back for some reason a little higher, and place underneath him several folded sheets.
Then stand to the left of him, and command the assistant to stand to the right of him, who should extend his arm to one side of the bowels and to the top of the navel.
Then take a pointed instrument and cut the diaphragm of the bowels in the middle part, cutting it along its length through the pentangular.
And let the incision be made according to the straightness equally distant from the line that must be observed between the skin of the bowels, so that it reaches the white diaphragm.
Excorate it, and observe, and be careful so that you do not insert anything into it; and your excising with which you exciate it according to the part that is suspended by the bowels, examine closely by excising according to the amount that is possible for you.
Then pierce the lower diaphragm with a wide incision, and extract all the moisture.
Then separate between the two lips of the incision with hooks, and stretch the diaphragm above them; and do not touch the bowels contained, and insert the diaphragm in that way that is possible for you. Then insert it completely or in pieces, and especially with its sides very fine; for if you do not examine the incision of it thoroughly, there is no security that the moisture will not return.
But if you notice that it has protruded beyond the edge of its sheath during your operation, then when you have finished cutting the scrotum, return it inside and sew up the two lips of the scrotum of the testicles with a suture, and treat it as you would any other wound until it is healed.
And if you find the testicle corrupted by some other disease, then cut the vessels which are above the suspensory ligament, extract the testicle and treat it as we have said.
But if the hernia is divided into two parts, then know that there are two hernias; therefore incise that part according as you have done in the other, and if it appears to you to be one operation, then perform it.
And you should clean the blood and insert into the incisions wool which is soaked in oil or rose oil; and place outside another piece of wool which is soaked in wine and oil, and spread this over both testicles and the abdomen; and place over it folded sheets and powdery lint, and tie those over with a ligature which is according to this form:
and two sheets should be pressed and filled with wool dyed red according to this shape; and the extremities with which it is tied up should be made of gut or of wet wool, and they should be attached by a string to the waistband of the trousers, and one extremity should go from behind between the buttocks and the second should go to the front part of the scrotum, and two extremities on each thigh and two other extremities on both sides of the groin, and all of the string should be tightened at the waistband of the trousers.
And sometimes this hernia is treated artificially by cautery instead of cutting with an iron; and you should take a thin scalpel and cut the scrotum of the testicles, and ignite it according to what we have recommended until the white sac containing the testicle is uncovered, and then you should apply cautery according to this form: and it is similar to the Greek letter alpha.
And you should pierce with that scalpel and ignite it until all of the moisture has been driven out.
And you should extend the scrotum with tongs and scrape it with tongs, and scrape with a small cautery which is ignited; and incise it according as it is possible for you to do so until you have eradicated all of it; and beware that the fire does not touch the testicle.
And know that this operation is more safe and more distant from blood flow, and better than an operation with cutting.
But if you experience an ulcer during cutting or cautery, or blood flow, then know that you should treat the ulcer according to what it requires with treatment which is suitable for it according to what has been said.
But if the patient is cowardly and does not expect a second operation because of its horrible nature, then you should perform piercing according to what I have recommended when it has been certified by you, through what has been said about the signs, that the hernia is fluid.
Then you should have the patient lie on his back on a high bed, and pierce the ulcer in the lowest part of it with a broad spear, and make the piercing according to the length of the body.
And the aperture should be ample so that all of the fluid runs out.
And you should place gut and ligature over it and leave it there so that the rest of the fluid runs out. And you should treat it until the wound is healed.
But if there is resistance to the discharge of the fluid when you pierce it: and this does not occur unless the white membrane in the orifice of the wound causes resistance and prohibits the exit of the fluid, then you should insert into the wound a peg or instrument by which the fluid is extracted from the hydrocele, the shape of which has been described; or attach to the compression of the hydrocele a small.
And know that the fluid returns and is accumulated again after about a month or so; and when it has been accumulated, then it should be pierced according to that same manner, for the patient will pass his days like this.
Chapter 63.
On cutting on a fleshy hernia and its treatment.
Know that in cutting on this hernia there is great fear of death in the greater dispositions; for I have seen the discharge of it and the patient saved by it.
And I am remembering the operation on that one and the properties of ulcers.
Therefore, I say that ulcers arise in the bodies of which the testicles are composed and are caused by many causes: or by acute sharp superfluity, which is distributed to the testicles, or by impact.
And the color of the ulcer is according to the color of the body, and there is not pain in it, and it is a heavy ulcer.
And its surface is smooth, of which the color is dark, and there is no feeling to it.
And sometimes it is caused by constriction of the vessels, and by inflammation of those thus, as has been perceived by memory of it, or by inflammation of veins.
But that which is caused by inflammation of vessels is known by the distribution of the ulcer when you compress it with your fingers; and there should not be touch to it.
But that which is caused by inflammation of a vein is not distributed from it because of compression with the fingers.
And it is possible that on this kind there should be cutting and on the other meats; and you should cut the scrotum of the testicles, and then extend the testicle to the parts above it, and extract it from the white sac, and ligate the suspensory ligament of the vessels, and incise the suspensory more so that you can extract it from all parts of the testicle.
Therefore if the hydrocele has become consolidated with those meats, then you should extract the hydrocele and incise it.
And if there is adhesions for some cause from the scrotum, or between that which is between the vessels, then you should loosen all of that adhesion and incise it with a round incision.
But if there is generation of flesh in the place of the adhesions which are behind, then you should incise all that is of it and extract the hydrocele as we have said.
Therefore when your operation is completed, then fill the wound with wool soaked in rose oil and wine; and you should treat it with the other treatment until it is healed.

Chapter 65:
On the treatment of intestinal hernias.
The occurrence of this hernia is due to an opening that extends in the chest towards the abdomen from the angles of the navel, so that when the intestines are pushed through that rupture into any of the intestines.
And this rupture is either from the chest or from an opening in it, and these two species occur for various reasons: by percussion, or by blows, or by crying, or by the elevation of some heavy cause, or by similarities.
And the sign of this, when it is from the extension of the chest, is that it occurs gradually over a long time, and does not occur suddenly, and it is a suppurative ulcer inside the abdomen because the chest compresses the intestine.
And the sign of it is when it is from an opening in the chest; because at the beginning it causes violent pain suddenly; and it is a diverse ulcer apparent below the apparent armpit, and this is due to the displacement of the intestine, and its body towards the parts outside the chest.
And sometimes it is pushed out with the intestine, and this hernia is called intestinal hernia.
And sometimes it is made with a hernia sac, and sometimes a hole in the intestine, and here it is retained, and this causes great harm to the patient, and sometimes it causes bad pain and especially when it is pressed.
And in the treatment of these species of this illness with iron there is fear, because one must avoid the formation in it.
And the way of performing this operation is to command the patient to draw in the intestine with his hand towards its cavity if he obeys its return, and then let him lie on his side between your hands, and lift his legs.
And then you will bring the armpit which connects with the armpit of the testicles upwards, and you will open the armpit entirely throughout its length; and you will put nails in two lips of the opening according to what you command them to open it with.
And if the opening according to the quantity that is possible for you, that from that the sac is pushed out.
And then you will cut away those chest muscles which are under the armpit of the testicles, until the white hard chest muscle is uncovered in each part.
Then you will put your finger into that which connects the testicle, in that which is between the white chest and the second chest, and you will free with it the adhesion which is in the part behind the sac.
And then you will draw with your hand the armpit of the testicles upwards, and you will extend the white chest towards it with your left hand, and lift the sac with the chest to the opening of the incision; and you will command the assistant to extend the sac towards you, and you will dissolve the adhesion behind it with a completed solution.
And you must pay attention with your fingers that there is no cause for the intestine to be wrapped in the white hard chest. But if you find any cause for it, then you will push it back down into the abdomen.
And then you will insert in the part under the armpit of the testicles by an incision from which blood and pus flow as we have mentioned in what we have said.
And then you will administer wool soaked in oil, and pause it over the ulcer; and administer the ligature which we have recommended (and sometimes the white chest is cauterized, which we have said about the incision of it fears a flow of blood, because many times they occur there), and let the ligature fall so that by itself it will close.
But if its closing is delayed, then have water heated, and pause it over that so that it falls according to what we have said.
And then cure the ulcer with the other cure of ulcers where it is healthy.
Chapter 66:
On hernia sac.
In this hernia, there is no one who has been cured with the treatment of it with iron.
And the first thing that is done as we have recommended in the hernia which is with a sac; and then you will tie the intestines over that incision with ease of it; and then dry in the middle around the ulcer with that which causes that, from which the intestines fall out.
And cure the ulcer as we have said so that it is healthy.
Chapter 67:
On the rupture which is made in the angles.
Sometimes there is a rupture in the angles as we have said, and it emerges from the place.
And do not allow any cause of the intestines to the genitals; and if it occurs, that is rare; and return it in all hours.
But if the time is prolonged with that, it is a fracture in the chest from which the intestine emerges in the chest; and this occurs because of the extension of the chest which is in the angles as we have said, which cause is because the chest is extended, and then it becomes soft and the place is suppurative and emerges.
And its cure is with cautery as it is preceded by the narratio of it.
And sometimes it is cured with iron in this way: and the patient hangs over his chest between your hands, and then drys the place of the rupture of the suppuratives emerging from incision according to the length of three fingers.
And then tightly tie the white bandage that is under the cord until it is exposed.
And then take the thread and place it over the prominent part of the wound, and press it to the abdomen.
And then sew the two prominent ends of the wound with the thread, joining one end to the other.
And then pull the end of the thread, but do not cut the bandage at all, nor stretch it out, nor any other cause that you know about in the treatment of intestinal hernias.
And then treat that with the treatment of ulcers, and when you insert the gallbladder, cleanse it and restore the ulcer until it is consolidated; for the bandage is contracted and the prominence of the rupture is not tightened.
And cautery is better in this place, because it is closer to health.
Chapter 68:
On the softening of the cords of the testes.
Many times the cords of the testes in some men are softened because the flesh that is between them is softened, and the guarding of it is weakened.
Therefore, it is necessary for the person treating the patient to make him lie on his back, and insert all of the softened cord along the natural cord; and then sew two lips with thread.
And if you want, sew up the superfluity of the softened cord in three or four places and with a firm stitch.
And then insert between the stitches; and then treat by the treatment of other ulcers until it is healed and the gallbladders fall out.
Chapter 69:
On castration.
Know that castration in our law is excommunicated, but for two reasons it has been related to me in this book: the first is so that the doctor who is questioned about it knows its treatment, and the second reason is that many times we have needed to castrate other beasts for our own purposes, like horses, oxen, pigs, and similar animals.
And so I say that castration is done in two ways: either by crushing or by cutting through.
But in the method that is done by crushing, the procedure is to make the beast defecate in warm water until its testicles are softened and hang down. And then grab those with your hand until they are dissolved and do not appear below the touch.
But in castration done by cutting and sectioning, you must hold the beast and squeeze the cord of its testicles with your left hand.
And then cut through the suspensory ligament and insert between each pair of processes with one cut until there are two holes.
And then insert those more that you have cut off. And do not leave any cause on the bandage over them, but only the thin bandage which is over the veins.
And this method of castration is better which is done by crushing, because crushing strongly leaves no cause in the testicles so that the beast desires copulation.
And then treat the ulcer until it is healed.
Chapter 70:
On the treatment of hermaphrodites.
Hermaphrodites in men are of two kinds: the first is when there appears an orifice between the cords of the testes, where there is a figure like that of a woman’s vulva between the two testicles.
And sometimes from it urine flows from the cord of the testicles.
But in women there is only one type: and it is that the clitoris on the foreskin is like two testicles of a man, a little of everything at the beginning of the foreskin like the foreskin of a man and two testicles.
And the treatment is of three kinds: two from men and one from women. And it is that you insert those tight flesh until the impression of that flows out, and then treat those with the treatment of other ulcers.
And in the second kind of men from whom urine flows from the cord of the testicles, there is no treatment or operation for it.
Chapter 71:
On the hymen and prominent flesh due to causes in women.
The strong hymen is tightly attached to natural causes so that it is pressed and made thin the guarding; and in some women it is enlarged so much that it is stretched like men and can enter into intercourse.
Therefore, you must grab the superfluity of the hymen with your hand or with a needle and insert it.
And do not pierce in the incision, especially in the part of the vein, so that no blood flow ensues.
And then treat that with the treatment of ulcers until it is healed.
But born flesh is flesh that grows in the womb of the mother to fill it, and very often it grows out from the foreskin according to the appearance of a snake (and because of this some call this “tail-like hermaphrodite”); therefore we must insert it like an hymen and treat it until it is healed.
Chapter 72:
On the treatment of syphilis.
Syphilis is when the clitoris of a woman is not perforated, or it is a small wound. And it can be natural or accidental.
Accidental is due to a wound that has preceded it, and that is caused by tightly bound flesh or a thin bandage or membrane.
And it is caused either in the womb or the bones of it, or in the supine part of it, or in the lower part of it, and strongly prohibits copulation and pregnancy, and very often the menstruation.
And the diagnosis of it is made by the guarding of the midwife, if the oppression is evident, then you must cover it with bandages; but if it is not evident, then you should draw it with your fingers or with a thread.
But if the oppression is due to a thin bandage and is prominent between the two lips, then you must cut and rupture it.
And so that it rests on both lips, and then rest your fingers from both sides and press them inwards.
And let the woman be on her back with her legs extended, and then extend both lips with force so that the thin bandage is broken and the oppression opened.
And then take wool and dip it in oil and place it over the wound, and anoint it with ointment every day until the wound is healed.
But if the bandage is thick and tough, then you must insert it with liniment of lat or myrrh resin.
But if the oppression is due to bound flesh, then suspend that with a thread and insert it.
Let them be the medicines that cause bleeding to stop, like aconite, and dragon’s blood, and alder, bound with egg white.
And then administer a wide lead cane for so that the wound is not healed loosely.
And hold it for several days and give it cool water of lye.
And then let it be healed by the other treatment of consolidation until it is healed.
And sometimes accidents happen in the great conception of other meats, and then they are conceived according to this manner. But if it is by the ulcer of the bone, then do not do any opposition to the ulcer of the bone in any way.
Chapter 73.
Of the cure of hemorrhoids, and of tail and red buttock which happen in the vagina of women.
Hemorrhoids are an obstruction of the orifices of many veins from which much blood flows continuously, and when hemorrhoids become old and are formed.
And I have already said in the division of them the species and signs of them, and thus say those who receive a cure and those that do not receive a cure.
I say therefore hemorrhoids and theyls when they are in the depth of the vagina and do not appear to the senses, then in these there shall be no cure made by iron.
But those which are in the opening of the vagina upon which one can see with senses, these are those which are cured.
And cause the woman to be in a hot bath and then extend it with tweezers or with rough cloth, and insert those with roots.
And then powder over them one of the insulating powders without biting, thus with aconite and similar to these.
Then put in a pouch their feet for an hour and then place that in cold water.
And if the flow of blood continues then do that in a decoction of cummin and of onion peels and of pomegranate peels and of similar things.
And take wheat flour and cook it with honey and sour wine and make a poultice with that over the back of it.
And if the blood has dried out then it is good; and if not then attach with two leeches and at the breasts no scarification.
And take wool and immerse that in juice of coriander or in juice of marigold or in juice of wild garlic with red wine and make that adhere to the place until it is healed. And cure the place with ointments until it is healed.
And cure it until it is healed.
Chapter 74.

Many species of ulcers happen in the vagina, thus with bone ulcer and ulcerous ulcer and suppuration and wormy and ragged and others ulcers. And I have already said these diseases and the species of them and their signs and their cures in the division.

And then cause you to make the woman lie on one side with her two sides; and recline on her back and join her feet to the part lower than the belly, and let her thighs be extended, and pause her arms under her elbows and let each hold according to what is convenient.

Chapter 75.
To teach midwives in what manner the children will be medicated when they come according to non-natural figure.
A necessary cause is that the midwife knows in the beginning the figure of the child's coming according to its signs and it is that when you see the woman pressing on her parts below and wanting to smell the air, and when she is eased by what is above her and the part is made easy for her, and hastens the exit of the child, then know that this part is according to a natural figure, and the exit of it upon its head, and the second one with that or suspended from the navel.
Therefore when you see these signs then cause the belly to be pressed so that the embryo descends gently when he comes out upon his head, and let the second one come with that or suspended from the navel, and it is cleaned of those superfluities by a good cleaning.
But that which is another of this part is non-natural and not laudable when the child comes out upon his feet and his body before his head, and his mother's hand or on his foot.I. Or is come out the head of it and his mother's hand or to its belly and bent it is converted over his neck and similar to the figures of it non-laudable.
A necessary cause is that the midwife be wise and subtle in all those causes, and that she guard against error and deception.
And I show you the entire figure of those, and what craft is in them so that it be signified by that and is laid upon that.
When the child is come out upon his head by natural force and that is violent upon the woman and it is made for him a difficult part, then cause that to be done, or that women hold it, and evaporate the depth of it with fenugreek cooked and with oiled herbs.
And then the midwife put between her fingers a little broad sponge and split it with that the second one, or dry that with its nail until she comes upon what is in her of humidity. And press on the woman's abdomen where the fetus is descending.
But if it does not descend, then the woman should be anointed with an ointment of linseed and fennel seed mixed together.
Then command him, the one performing the anointing, to apply pressure and make the mother sneeze with the mixture; and hold her mouth and nose for an hour so that the fetus will come out quickly.
And if both hands of the fetus are not coming out at the beginning, then you should gently pull them out little by little. But if the fetus does not respond to the instrument, then place the woman on a board and lift her feet up, and gently rock the board back and forth on the ground; and the woman should be held so that she does not fall off the board due to the rocking.
And if the hands are not bent back and the fetus is not born, then insert your hand inside and break the fetus's head or grab its body with a cloth and pull it out little by little; for in this way, it will come out.
When the fetus is on their feet, then you should gently push those up and turn the fetus a little, and suck it in, and grab one of its feet and pull it gently.
But when it has come out between the thighs, then you command him to push it out, and make the mother sneeze with the mixture; for it will come out if God wills it.
And if it is not born with what we have described, then you gently return the fetus little by little to where it was, for it will come out more easily with its natural movement.
And if it is not possible with all that we have described, then take myrrh and dissolved gum, and pound them well in the mortar, and apply this to the woman's vagina, at the bottom of her abdomen. Then make her drink tepid water while she is achieving the vapor bath.
And when his feet are softened, then you give him the smoke of myrrh and place it under him. And when she has been in the smoke for an hour, then you make her lie down on a board and make her sneeze and open her mouth, and lift up the lower part of her abdomen with gentle pressure, for the fetus will come out at once.
Delivery of the fetus hanging down by one of its hands. You should gently pull the hand and suck in the fetus little by little; but if you cannot reduce it, then lift up the woman and make her walk.
And if she cannot walk, then make her lie down on the ground and rock her thighs with violent movement; and you should administer to her any remedies that are given by doctors made from mucilage.
And if the delivery has come, then make her lie down on a board and study the hand's reduction and suck in the fetus according to its natural shape, and make the woman sneeze and command him to push so that it will be born.
Delivery of the fetus on the neck with its hands and face spread out and the fetus' face towards the mother's back. Then the midwife should hold the fetus' hand and gently turn it little by little, and this will be easier.
And when it is turned and how it is sucked in, then you apply to its head what we have recommended of oil and mucilage.
Then command him to grab his mother' hand little by little, and when you have done this, then make her lie down on a board and command him to be bent over the right side, and command him to push; and make the woman sneeze with the mixture. Exit of the fetus prepared on its side.
When it comes out of the mother' body in this way, consider and then you insert your finger inside so that it is evacuated from moisture.
And if the fetus is suspended over its face and neck, then you insert your finger inside so that it is not retained and delayed.
Then you gently push the fetus to the sides so that it hangs down as you want, and command the woman to push several times; for it will come out with easy delivery if God wills it.
Exit of twins or multiple fetuses. Know that twins are born many times, and sometimes there are three or four; but this is strange and rare, and it does not live.
And count them; and if they are multiple, there is a second one, and they are separated by the umbilical cord, distinguish those inside the navel of each one of them; and sometimes they are born like this with easy delivery, and sometimes with delivery that is not possible as we have recommended.
And if they are difficult to deliver and come to what we have said about the non-natural shapes, then you cure them as we have recorded.
And if the midwife does what she does with ease and subtlety, and delays, and it is made according to all the forms as it is prepared for him by bringing health.
Remember that which is formed in the womb from embryos and abortions.
Some are formed in the womb one, two, three, four, five, six, seven, and even ten; and I have verily seen a woman bear six, and another ten, all formed, which cause was made through measurement by the glorious wise ones.
And know that it is in the science of the midwife that which is strong for her to approach this little one like that, and therefore stop it from doing so.
Chapter .lxxvi.
On the extraction of the fetus when it is dead.
When you treat the dead fetus with what we have said in the division of medicine and it is not yet out, then you should consider if the woman is of sound health and not of any of the accidents by which she is feared to suffer harm.
Then you should have the woman bent over her chest and her head bent down, and her thighs elevated.
And the midwife should hold that in two parts or be tied in such a way that the body of the fetus does not extend because of the extraction of the fetus.
And then you moisten the mouth of the patient with moist oil and with mucilage of alder, fenugreek, and seeds of it.
And then the midwife anoints her hand with those oils and mucilage, and then inserts her hand smoothly into the vagina, and then seeks with her hand the place where the nails are in the foot.
And if it is convenient in that case: then you consider whether the foot is prepared so that it descends over his head, and then you place the nails in his heels, or on his neck, or in his mouth, or in his palate, or under his beard, or in the hollow of his chest, or under his armpits.
But if the descent is on his feet, then it is in the instep, or in the middle of his back.
And whoever has the nail holds it with his right hand, and places its curve in that place which is between the fingers of his left hand, and inserts his hand smoothly and puts the nail in one of those places we have mentioned, until he reaches the true cause.
And then place and fix in the aperture of him another nail, or a third if necessary, so that there is an equal attraction, and not extension according to his rectitude only.
But let the mouth be opened to its full extent, so that the extraction of it is facilitated as it is done in a tooth that is pulled out.
And whoever in him that is between them let the extension be softened; and if any part of him is retained, then let the midwife anoint one of her fingers with oil, and insert that skillfully and turn it about with what is retained.
So if the part of the foot is dislocated, then let the nails be interchanged into a place that is higher; and do this as long as all of the foot is dislocated.
But if the hand is dislocated in front of the other, and it is not possible to reduce that by compressing it, then let a bandage be wrapped around that; and then extract that as long as all of it is dislocated, and insert it into the joint of the hand or in the elbow.
And do this also to the other hand and the two feet.
But if the head of the foot is large, or there happens to it compression in its extraction, or there is some constriction on him, then let the midwife insert between the fingers a spatulate and pointed instrument and split the head and extract the fluid, or discover that with an instrument which is named 'alundat', the shape of which will come with the shapes of the other instruments in the chapter which is to come.
And likewise do if the foot is of a large head by nature: and then let him insert that with a ligature, or take it with an awl as we have said; and then extract the bones with forceps.
And if the head is dislocated and there is constriction due to the collarbone, then let it be split so that the moisture which is in the foot be discharged.
But if it is not complicated, nor obstinate in its dislocation, then you insert the head immediately as soon as possible to you.
And if the hernia of the abdomen is ulcerated or is dropping out, then let you pierce that so that the fluid that is in it runs out.
But if the foot is on his feet, then the attraction of it is greater and the direction of it to the mouth of the vagina is farther.
But if it is constricted due to the abdomen and the foot, then let you extract that with a bandage which you will have wrapped around your hand, and split the abdomen and the foot so that what is in them runs out.
But if the other members stand and turn the head, then the midwife inserts her left hand; but if the mouth of the vagina is open, then she inserts her hand in the anus of air, and seeks with that the head, and pulls it with her fingers into the mouth of the vagina, and then inserts into him a nail, or two nails, and pulls him with those.
And if the mouth of the vagina is constricted by an ulcer that comes to the u, then let it not be rubbed on him; but beforehand let the flow of moistening fatty causes be administered. And administer plasters; and follow the patient with waters that soften and moisten.
And if the foot is on his side, then if possible let it be turned; and let what we have said about the living foot be administered to him.
And if that is not possible, then let it be inserted into wooden stakes, and extracted.
And let there not remain any cause inside the secondina.
And when you have completed all your operation, then administer what we have said about the cure in ulcerated cauteries that come from the vagina.
And if there comes blood flow, then let it be stopped with astringent waters and administer the other cure.
And I have already seen a woman in whose abdomen was a dead fetus, and then over that other fire burning, and then the dead fire is the other fetus. There happened to him an ulcer in his groin; and it was swollen so that fire broke out, and he began to vomit blood.
And I was called to his cure, and medicated him for a long time, and the ulcer was not healed.
Then I applied to him some plasters of strong attraction, and extracted from him a bone, and then passed some days, and extracted another bone; and I was very marvelled, since there was not bone in the abdomen.
And then I thought that they were the bones of the dead fetus.
Then I cut the ulcer, and extracted from him some bones, the woman having remained in the same disposition, and already lived for a long time, a little of the blood flowing.
And I did not think that anything was strange except that in it is science and aid to what the doctor artifices with his hand for cure administers.
Of the forms of the instruments which are necessary to extract the fetus.
Form of vertigine with which is open the vagina:
This is the form of straitness in which are engaged the lips, to that engagement are two virtues in two extremes of two parts. But this virtue let it be more subtle of compression, and let it be made of ebony or of wood of boxwood.
And let the thickness of each wood be as two fingers and the margin of either side is one finger, and the length of each is a palm and a half; and in the middle part of two woods are two joints of that woods which are already fitted, of which the length is the measure of a palm and a little more, and the thickness of each is as two fingers, or a little more.
And these two additions are inserted into the mouth of the vagina so that it is open by them when you turn the two prescribed straitnesses.
Other form also similar to that more subtle and farther:
Let it be made of boxwood or of ebony according to the likeness of forceps. But in the end of it are two additions thus with handles, and the length of those additions is as a palm, and the thickness of each is two fingers.
And when you want to open the womb, then you should let the woman lie on her back with her feet hanging down, and open what is between their thighs. Then open your hand with the instrument as you would with forceps according to the amount that you want from the opening of the womb while the midwife does what you ask.

Form of delivery by force in which the fetus is forced out:
Form of extraction with a large head
And it is similar to forceps which have teeth at the end, and sometimes it is made long like forceps according to this form, and sometimes with teeth like a pair of jaws with which it is cut and crushed. Form of extraction of a few:
Form having one thorn:
Form of one thorn having two thorns:
Form of spatula having two ends, with which the head is cut off:
Form of two wide spatulas:
All those instruments are exercised, and when they are more numerous and prepared by the artisans, then they are easier for the artisan and better for men because of their quantity.
And whether you have any of those instruments or not, you should be prepared, because the need for them is inexcusable.
Of extraction of the placenta.
When the placenta is retained after childbirth, then you should command the woman to retain her breath, and then make her sneeze with cinnamon, and press your hand over her mouth and nose, and if she vomits it out, that's good.
And if not, then you take a bowl and pierce the lining with a knife, and place in it herbs that burn the mouth of the womb, such as hellebore and ruda and anise and camomile and scilla and arabic hellebore and cassia wood and sanderswood. All these herbs or some of them are submerged in water in the bowl, and place that over the fire.
And then place a straw in the woman's mouth, and hold that while the evaporation comes into the cavity of the womb.
And then make her sneeze as we have said, and the placenta will be forced out with speed.
But if this cure does not work and it has not come out, then command the midwife to submerge her left hand in sesame oil or in mullein, and then insert that in the vagina and scratch with that the placenta, and when you have found the placenta, take hold of it and pull it out little by little according to rectitude so that the woman does not feel too much pain. Before this, make sure that it is moved to the right and left sides with ease.
And if the mouth of the womb is narrow, we have already recommended the cure with sneezing and medication in the bowl with herbs.
But if it is not forced out with all the causes that we have recommended, then be careful that you do not tire too much on her in iteration of abstraction, but instead what comes out of her mouth lies in the woman's lap, and then close up that with ointment and tetrafarmacon; because that will cause to rot that, then dissolved and forced out.
But when it is rotten, there comes from it a bad odor to the head and stomach, and then what the woman vomits out lies in her lap; and then let there be administered sub-fumigations and convenient things for that.
But some of the Ancients have already tested sub-fumigation of netherwort and of dry figs.
Form of instrument by which the woman is sub-fumigated because of retention of menstruation and of the placenta:
It is made of brass or copper.
And the thin end is placed in the vagina and the wide end over the fire, and the sub-fumigation is held over the coals of the fire.
And hold that while the sub-fumigation is consumed and iterate another.
Of cure of the anus of a child not pierced.
Move children who are born and whose anuses are not pierced, which cause pain and are swollen. Then let the midwife pierce that with her finger; and if not, pierce that with a pointed spatula, and be careful that it does not touch the clitoris.
And then place over that wool soaked in wine and oil, and cure that with ointment until it is healed.
But if you fear that it is swollen, then place in the slit a straw for several days, and hold it when the child wants to urinate.
And then it happens that the swelling of the anus comes from hardening of a boil or abscess; therefore let that hardening be lanced, and then cure that with what we have said about the cure and the poultice.
Of cure for fistulas that come from below.
The fistulas that come from below in the perineum are low and thick, which come out near the anus or in the space between the parts.
And it is a fistula or many.
And when that hardening becomes old and corrupt by the moist white or purulent discharge, and sometimes these fistulas penetrate some.
And those that penetrate are known by what comes out of them through the opening and by flatulence; and sometimes the woman vomits, and very often it comes out of them vermin.
And sometimes those fistulas penetrate into the bladder, and into the flesh of the vagina; and sometimes they penetrate into the junction of the hip and into the notch of the anus.
And that in which the fistula penetrates into the anus but does not penetrate is that you put your finger into the anus and insert a pointed probe of brass or iron into the fistula when it is tense.
But if in that it is tense, then insert into that a probe of lead or of horsehair until you feel the probe or the bristle in your finger.
And if you do not feel anything in it nor any sign of discharge or worm or flatulence, as we have said, then know that it is not penetrated, and then go to the cure.
And when the fistula penetrates into the bladder or into the flesh of the vagina, then its sign is emission of urine from that and prohibition of that towards that which the place is medicated with ointment.
But if it penetrates into the hip joint or into the bone and causes pain in the circuit of the perineum; and its sign is that the probe goes through there if in it is not tense within the bone, and pain in the circuit of the perineum; and when there is no discharge from there, nor worm, nor flatulence, as we have said, then know that it is not healed with ointment.
And in all those fistulas there is not a complete cure, and the cure of those is work and labor of the physicians over it who are firmly set.
But in that which is not penetrating and not old, healing with iron is expected according to what I have told you, and that which I have already tried.
And let the patient lie on his back and raise his legs up against his chest, with his thighs bent towards his belly, and then insert a probe of lead or of copper into the wound if it is a tortuous fistula, and feel around to find the place where the probe enters.
And if the patient is suffering from a hernia in his neck, then you must push your index finger into his neck.
And if you feel the probe pushing itself in through the opening when you insert it with your finger, then you know for certain that this is a penetrable hernia; and so you should not operate on it, for there will be no cure, as we have said.
But some people say that this kind of hernia is curable in certain individuals who are thin.
And the treatment by which recovery is expected in such a case is that you apply a subtle cautery according to the size of the fistula, as mentioned before, and insert this cautery into the hernia around the neck; then repeat this twice or thrice until you know that all the flesh around the hernia, which resembles a feather reed, has been tightened.
And then treat it with poultices wrapped in cloth until all the flesh around the hernia has healed; and treat the hernia itself with medicines that generate and solidify flesh, and if it is cured, well and good; but if not, no other cure will help.

And then clean off the flesh around the hernia which resembles a feather reed, and none of these things should break open.

And then treat the hernia with poultices wrapped in cloth or in cheesecloth until the swelling goes down; and then cure the wound with a ointment that generates hard flesh and solidifies it.
And this is how medicines which have astringent and drying properties work: when the swelling has been restored, then it is healed and you need not fear recurrence.
But if the hernia has permeated into the rectum and is elongated from there to the surface of the body, then insert your index finger into the anus and feel around with it.
And if you feel the probe and between you and it there is membrane or flesh, and it is close to being penetrable, then this hernia should not be operated on by a direct approach, but only according to the way of confidence and hope.
This can be done in three ways: either by cauterizing it as we have said; or by drying up the hernia so that you achieve its cavity and it is possible for you to insert instruments and perform the cure close to the hernia; or by not cutting into the membrane which contains the neck, but by having the patient lean forward from the waist so that the hernia slides down away from the neck without his will, and then cure the hernia as we have said since it is very easy to heal; or by elongating this membrane and cleaning out the pus which has dried up around the anus, using a probe or some other instrument with a sharp end, and then clean off the flesh around the hernia which has been cut through at the place where you can pierce it by pushing in; and then strive to make the whole wound heal by cutting, and if the orifice above is not solidified and the fistula remains open at the anus, then pus will flow out through the hernia. Of suturing up hemorrhoids from which blood flows when they are cut.
Hemorrhoids occur in two ways, for either they are between the anus like charcoal or they are like grass with fat on top. And some are small and large, and the blood flows from them at times; they are raised up and are around the anus and at its edges.
But those which are outside the anus are according to the months of little moisture; from them flows water with a little blood, and they are according to the colour of the body.
And the cure for those which are inside the neck is to command the patient to sit up and to press in so that the neck dries out and the hemorrhoids appear to you. Then you must pinch and suspend them with your nails or what you have those with your fingernail, and then cut off their roots.
But if the nails are not gripped in them due to their moisture and softness, then take those with a rough cloth or a cord or a strip of wool, and pull them out with your fingers, and then insert them and sprinkle some powdered caustic on them over the cut, so that they are as cauterized; or cauterize them as mentioned in the chapter on cauterizing. And then cure them with the other cure so that they heal.
And if the anus does not obey the exit, then castor the patient with castoreum in which there is a small bite, and let it be washed with that which is in the neck and let it obey the exit gently when the patient is squeezed.
But if the hemorrhoids are outside the anus, then their cause is looseness, and you must take them with your fingernail or with a needle, and insert them, and then cure them as we have said so that they heal.

Warts are small, rough, round, and fistulous protuberances on the surface of the body, and they often occur in children's hands.
And its treatment is that you stretch it out and pierce it, or tighten it with gut or string so that it falls off. And if you wish, cauterize it with fire or sharp medicine.
